      <p><b>Japan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span lang="ja">日本</span>, <i>Nippon</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Japanese" title="Help:IPA/Japanese">[ɲippoꜜɴ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ja-nippon(%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC).ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Ja-nippon%28%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%29.ogg" class="internal" title="Ja-nippon(日本).ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span> or <i>Nihon</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Japanese" title="Help:IPA/Japanese">[ɲihoꜜɴ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ja-nihon(%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC).ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/92/Ja-nihon%28%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%29.ogg" class="internal" title="Ja-nihon(日本).ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, located in the northwest <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. It is bordered on the west by the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a>, and extends from the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> in the north toward the <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> in the south. Part of the <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a>, Japan spans <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">an archipelago</a> of <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Japan" title="List of islands of Japan">6852 islands</a> covering 377,975 square kilometers (145,937&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi); the five main islands are <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shikoku" title="Shikoku">Shikoku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Island" title="Okinawa Island">Okinawa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> is Japan's capital and largest city; other major cities include <a href="/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">Yokohama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fukuoka" title="Fukuoka">Fukuoka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kobe" title="Kobe">Kobe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kyoto" title="Kyoto">Kyoto</a>. </p>
      <p>Japan is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">eleventh-most populous country</a> in the world, as well as one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population_density" title="List of countries and dependencies by population density">most densely populated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urbanization_by_country" title="Urbanization by country">urbanized</a>. About three-fourths of the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Japan" title="Geography of Japan">country's terrain</a> is mountainous, concentrating its population of 125.57 million on narrow coastal plains. Japan is divided into <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">47 administrative prefectures</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Japan" title="List of regions of Japan">eight traditional regions</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">most populous metropolitan area</a> in the world, with more than 37.4 million residents. </p>
      <p>Japan <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Paleolithic" title="Japanese Paleolithic">has been inhabited</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a> period (30,000 BC), though the first mentions of the archipelago appear in <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Han" title="Book of Han">Chinese chronicles</a> from the 1st century AD. Between the 4th and 9th centuries, the kingdoms of Japan became unified under an <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">emperor</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Imperial_House_of_Japan" title="Imperial House of Japan">imperial court</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Heian-ky%C5%8D" title="Heian-kyō">Heian-kyō</a>. Beginning in the 12th century, political power was held by a series of military dictators (<i><a href="/wiki/Shogun" title="Shogun">shōgun</a></i>) and feudal lords (<i><a href="/wiki/Daimyo" title="Daimyo">daimyō</a></i>), and enforced by a class of warrior nobility (<i><a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a></i>). After a <a href="/wiki/Sengoku_period" title="Sengoku period">century-long period of civil war</a>, the country was reunified in 1603 under the <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a>, which enacted an <a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">isolationist foreign policy</a>. In 1854, a <a href="/wiki/Perry_Expedition" title="Perry Expedition">United States fleet</a> forced Japan to <a href="/wiki/Bakumatsu" title="Bakumatsu">open trade to the West</a>, which led to <a href="/wiki/Boshin_War" title="Boshin War">the end of the shogunate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Restoration" title="Meiji Restoration">restoration of imperial power</a> in 1868. In the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_(era)" title="Meiji (era)">Meiji period</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> adopted a <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Constitution" title="Meiji Constitution">Western-styled constitution</a> and pursued a program of <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modernization_theory" title="Modernization theory">modernization</a>. In 1937, Japan <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">invaded China</a>; in 1941, it entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis power</a>. After suffering defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">two atomic bombings</a>, Japan <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrendered</a> in 1945 and came under a seven-year <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan" title="Occupation of Japan">Allied occupation</a>, during which it adopted a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Japan" title="Constitution of Japan">new constitution</a>. Since 1947, Japan has maintained a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> legislature, the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">National Diet</a>. </p>
      <p>Japan is a <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a> and a member of numerous international organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (since 1956), the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">Group of Seven</a>. Although it has <a href="/wiki/Article_9_of_the_Japanese_Constitution" title="Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution">renounced its right to declare war</a>, the country maintains <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Forces" title="Japan Self-Defense Forces">Self-Defense Forces</a> that are ranked as the world's <a href="/wiki/Military#Capability_development" title="Military">fourth-most powerful military</a>. After World War II, Japan experienced <a href="/wiki/Japanese_economic_miracle" title="Japanese economic miracle">high economic growth</a>, becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP" title="List of countries by largest historical GDP">second-largest economy</a> in the world by 1990 before being surpassed by China in 2010. Despite <a href="/wiki/Economic_stagnation" title="Economic stagnation">stagnant growth</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Lost_Decade_(Japan)" title="Lost Decade (Japan)">Lost Decade</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Japan" title="Economy of Japan">country's economy</a> remains the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">third-largest by nominal GDP</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">fourth-largest by PPP</a>. A leader in the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Japan" title="Automotive industry in Japan">automotive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry_in_Japan" title="Electronics industry in Japan">electronics industries</a>, Japan has made significant contributions to <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Japan" title="Science and technology in Japan">science and technology</a>. Ranked the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_in_Asia_and_Oceania_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries in Asia and Oceania by Human Development Index">second-highest country</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> in Asia after <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, Japan has the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">second-highest life expectancy</a>, though it is experiencing a <a href="/wiki/Aging_of_Japan" title="Aging of Japan">decline in population</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Japan" title="Culture of Japan">culture of Japan</a> is well-known around the world, including its <a href="/wiki/Japanese_art" title="Japanese art">art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Japan" title="Music of Japan">music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_popular_culture" title="Japanese popular culture">popular culture</a>, which encompasses prominent <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">animation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_games_in_Japan" title="Video games in Japan">video game</a> industries. </p>

           <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li> 
          </ul> </li> 
         <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a> 
          <ul> 
           <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Art_and_architecture"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Art and architecture</span></a></li> 
           <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Literature_and_philosophy"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Literature and philosophy</span></a></li> 
           <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Performing_arts"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Performing arts</span></a></li> 
           <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Customs_and_holidays"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Customs and holidays</span></a></li> 
           <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li> 
           <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">8.6</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>

          </ul> </li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Japan" title="Names of Japan">Names of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color:#b0c4de">Japan</th>
        </tr>
        <tr style="display:none;">
         <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #b0c4de;">Japanese name</th>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">Kanji</a></th>
         <td><span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%E5%9B%BD" class="extiw" title="wikt:日本国">日本国</a></span></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hiragana" title="Hiragana">Hiragana</a></th>
         <td><span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%81%AB%E3%81%A3%E3%81%BD%E3%82%93%E3%81%93%E3%81%8F" class="extiw" title="wikt:にっぽんこく">にっぽんこく</a><br><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%81%AB%E3%81%BB%E3%82%93%E3%81%93%E3%81%8F" class="extiw" title="wikt:にほんこく">にほんこく</a></span></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Katakana" title="Katakana">Katakana</a></th>
         <td><span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%83%8B%E3%83%83%E3%83%9D%E3%83%B3%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AF" class="extiw" title="wikt:ニッポンコク">ニッポンコク</a><br><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%83%8B%E3%83%9B%E3%83%B3%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AF" class="extiw" title="wikt:ニホンコク">ニホンコク</a></span></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
          <table class="collapsible collapsed" style="padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent">
           <tbody>
            <tr>
             <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 100%; text-align: left; background-color: #f9ffbc;">Transcriptions</th>
            </tr>
            <tr>
             <th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Japanese" title="Romanization of Japanese">Romanization</a></th>
             <td><span style="font-style: normal" lang="ja-Latn" title="Japanese-language romanization">Nippon-koku<br>Nihon-koku</span></td>
            </tr>
           </tbody>
          </table></td>
        </tr>
        <tr style="display:none">
         <td colspan="2"> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The name for Japan in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> is written using the <a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">kanji</a> <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text">日本</span></span> and pronounced <i>Nippon</i> or <i>Nihon</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-schreiber_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schreiber-10">[9]</a></sup> Before it was adopted in the early 8th century, the country was known in China as <i><a href="/wiki/Wa_(Japan)" title="Wa (Japan)">Wa</a></i> (<span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text">倭</span></span>) and in Japan by the <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a> <i>Yamato</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-carr_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carr-11">[10]</a></sup> <i>Nippon</i>, the original <a href="/wiki/Sino-Japanese_reading" class="mw-redirect" title="Sino-Japanese reading">Sino-Japanese reading</a> of the characters, is favored for official uses, including on <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">banknotes</a> and postage stamps.<sup id="cite_ref-schreiber_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schreiber-10">[9]</a></sup> <i>Nihon</i> is typically used in everyday speech and reflects shifts in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_phonology" title="Japanese phonology">Japanese phonology</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">Edo period</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-carr_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carr-11">[10]</a></sup> The characters <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text">日本</span></span> mean "sun origin".<sup id="cite_ref-schreiber_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schreiber-10">[9]</a></sup> It is the source of the popular Western <a href="/wiki/Epithet" title="Epithet">epithet</a> "Land of the Rising Sun".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The name <i>Japan</i> is based on the Chinese pronunciation and was introduced to European languages through early trade. In the 13th century, <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> recorded the early <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wu_Chinese" title="Wu Chinese">Wu Chinese</a> pronunciation of the characters <span lang="zh">日本國</span> as <i>Cipangu</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> The old <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> name for Japan, <i>Japang</i> or <i>Japun</i>, was borrowed from a southern coastal Chinese dialect and encountered by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> traders in Southeast Asia, who brought the word to Europe in the early 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> The first version of the name in English appears in a book published in 1577, which spelled the name as <i>Giapan</i> in a translation of a 1565 Portuguese letter.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Japan" title="History of Japan">History of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_to_classical_history">Prehistoric to classical history</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Emperor_Jimmu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emperor_Jimmu.jpg/170px-Emperor_Jimmu.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emperor_Jimmu.jpg/255px-Emperor_Jimmu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emperor_Jimmu.jpg/340px-Emperor_Jimmu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1242" data-file-height="1807"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Emperor_Jimmu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Legend" title="Legend">Legendary</a> <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Jimmu" title="Emperor Jimmu">Emperor Jimmu</a><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text">神武天皇</span>, <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Jinmu-tennō</i>)</span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Paleolithic" title="Japanese Paleolithic">Paleolithic culture</a> from around 30,000&nbsp;BC constitutes the first known habitation of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">islands of Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> This was followed from around 14,500&nbsp;BC (the start of the <a href="/wiki/J%C5%8Dmon_period" title="Jōmon period">Jōmon period</a>) by a <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> semi-sedentary <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> culture characterized by <a href="/wiki/Pit-house" title="Pit-house">pit dwelling</a> and rudimentary agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J%C5%8Dmon_pottery" title="Jōmon pottery">Clay vessels</a> from the period are among the oldest surviving examples of pottery.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> From around 1000 BC, <a href="/wiki/Yayoi_period#Origin_of_the_Yayoi_people" title="Yayoi period">Yayoi people</a> began to enter the archipelago from Kyushu, intermingling with the <a href="/wiki/Jomon_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Jomon people">Jōmon</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Yayoi_period" title="Yayoi period">Yayoi period</a> saw the introduction of practices including <a href="/wiki/Paddy_field" title="Paddy field">wet-rice farming</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> a new <a href="/wiki/Yayoi_pottery" title="Yayoi pottery">style of pottery</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> and metallurgy from China and Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> According to legend, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Jimmu" title="Emperor Jimmu">Emperor Jimmu</a> (grandson of <a href="/wiki/Amaterasu" title="Amaterasu">Amaterasu</a>) founded <a href="/wiki/Yamatai" title="Yamatai">a kingdom</a> in central Japan in 660 BC, beginning a <a href="/wiki/Imperial_House_of_Japan" title="Imperial House of Japan">continuous imperial line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan first appears in written history in the Chinese <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Han" title="Book of Han">Book of Han</a></i>, completed in 111 AD. Buddhism was introduced to Japan from <a href="/wiki/Baekje" title="Baekje">Baekje</a> (a Korean kingdom) in 552, but the development of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Japan" title="Buddhism in Japan">Japanese Buddhism</a> was primarily influenced by China.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> Despite early resistance, Buddhism was promoted by the ruling class, including figures like <a href="/wiki/Prince_Sh%C5%8Dtoku" title="Prince Shōtoku">Prince Shōtoku</a>, and gained widespread acceptance beginning in the <a href="/wiki/Asuka_period" title="Asuka period">Asuka period</a> (592–710).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The far-reaching <a href="/wiki/Taika_Reform" title="Taika Reform">Taika Reforms</a> in 645 nationalized all land in Japan, to be <a href="/wiki/Equal-field_system" title="Equal-field system">distributed equally</a> among cultivators, and ordered the compilation of a household registry as the basis for a new system of taxation.<sup id="cite_ref-Sansom_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sansom-27">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jinshin_War" title="Jinshin War">Jinshin War</a> of 672, a bloody conflict between <a href="/wiki/Prince_%C5%8Cama" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Ōama">Prince Ōama</a> and his nephew <a href="/wiki/Prince_%C5%8Ctomo" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Ōtomo">Prince Ōtomo</a>, became a major catalyst for further administrative reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-ritsuryo_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ritsuryo-28">[27]</a></sup> These reforms culminated with the promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Taih%C5%8D_Code" title="Taihō Code">Taihō Code</a>, which consolidated existing statutes and established the structure of the central and subordinate local governments.<sup id="cite_ref-Sansom_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sansom-27">[26]</a></sup> These legal reforms created the <i><a href="/wiki/Ritsury%C5%8D" title="Ritsuryō">ritsuryō</a></i> state, a system of Chinese-style centralized government that remained in place for half a millennium.<sup id="cite_ref-ritsuryo_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ritsuryo-28">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Nara_period" title="Nara period">Nara period</a> (710–784) marked the emergence of a Japanese state centered on the Imperial Court in <a href="/wiki/Heij%C5%8D_Palace" title="Heijō Palace">Heijō-kyō</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Nara,_Nara" class="mw-redirect" title="Nara, Nara">Nara</a>). The period is characterized by the appearance of a nascent <a href="/wiki/Japanese_literature" title="Japanese literature">literary culture</a> with the completion of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kojiki" title="Kojiki">Kojiki</a></i> (712) and <i><a href="/wiki/Nihon_Shoki" title="Nihon Shoki">Nihon Shoki</a></i> (720), as well as the development of Buddhist-inspired artwork and <a href="/wiki/Historic_Monuments_of_Ancient_Nara" title="Historic Monuments of Ancient Nara">architecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-courtiers_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courtiers-30">[29]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/735%E2%80%93737_Japanese_smallpox_epidemic" title="735–737 Japanese smallpox epidemic">smallpox epidemic in 735–737</a> is believed to have killed as much as one-third of Japan's population.<sup id="cite_ref-courtiers_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courtiers-30">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> In 784, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Kanmu" title="Emperor Kanmu">Emperor Kanmu</a> moved the capital, settling on <a href="/wiki/Heian-ky%C5%8D" title="Heian-kyō">Heian-kyō</a> (modern Kyoto) in 794.<sup id="cite_ref-courtiers_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courtiers-30">[29]</a></sup> This marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Heian_period" title="Heian period">Heian period</a> (794–1185), during which a distinctly indigenous Japanese culture emerged. <a href="/wiki/Murasaki_Shikibu" title="Murasaki Shikibu">Murasaki Shikibu</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_Genji" title="The Tale of Genji">The Tale of Genji</a></i> and the lyrics of Japan's national anthem "<a href="/wiki/Kimigayo" title="Kimigayo">Kimigayo</a>" were written during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feudal_era">Feudal era</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg/220px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg/330px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg/440px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3184" data-file-height="1461"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">Samurai</a> warriors battling Mongols during the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasions of Japan">Mongol invasions of Japan</a>, depicted in the <i><a href="/wiki/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba" title="Mōko Shūrai Ekotoba">Mōko Shūrai Ekotoba</a></i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan's feudal era was characterized by the emergence and dominance of a ruling class of warriors, the <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Leibo2015_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leibo2015-33">[32]</a></sup> In 1185, following the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Taira_clan" title="Taira clan">Taira clan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Genpei_War" title="Genpei War">Genpei War</a>, samurai <a href="/wiki/Minamoto_no_Yoritomo" title="Minamoto no Yoritomo">Minamoto no Yoritomo</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Military_government" title="Military government">military government</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kamakura,_Kanagawa" class="mw-redirect" title="Kamakura, Kanagawa">Kamakura</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> After Yoritomo's death, the <a href="/wiki/H%C5%8Dj%C5%8D_clan" title="Hōjō clan">Hōjō clan</a> came to power as regents for the <i>shōguns</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-courtiers_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courtiers-30">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Zen" title="Zen">Zen</a> school of Buddhism was introduced from China in the <a href="/wiki/Kamakura_period" title="Kamakura period">Kamakura period</a> (1185–1333) and became popular among the samurai class.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kamakura_shogunate" title="Kamakura shogunate">Kamakura shogunate</a> repelled <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasions of Japan">Mongol invasions</a> in 1274 and 1281 but was eventually <a href="/wiki/Kenmu_Restoration" title="Kenmu Restoration">overthrown</a> by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Go-Daigo" title="Emperor Go-Daigo">Emperor Go-Daigo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-courtiers_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courtiers-30">[29]</a></sup> Go-Daigo was defeated by <a href="/wiki/Ashikaga_Takauji" title="Ashikaga Takauji">Ashikaga Takauji</a> in 1336, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Muromachi_period" title="Muromachi period">Muromachi period</a> (1336–1573).<sup id="cite_ref-Shirane2012a_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shirane2012a-36">[35]</a></sup> The succeeding <a href="/wiki/Ashikaga_shogunate" title="Ashikaga shogunate">Ashikaga shogunate</a> failed to control the feudal warlords (<i>daimyōs</i>) and a <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cnin_War" title="Ōnin War">civil war began in 1467</a>, opening the century-long <a href="/wiki/Sengoku_period" title="Sengoku period">Sengoku period</a> ("Warring States").<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 16th century, Portuguese traders and <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> reached Japan for the first time, initiating direct <a href="/wiki/Nanban_trade" title="Nanban trade">commercial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanban_art" title="Nanban art">cultural</a> exchange between Japan and the West.<sup id="cite_ref-courtiers_30-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courtiers-30">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oda_Nobunaga" title="Oda Nobunaga">Oda Nobunaga</a> used European technology and firearms to conquer many other <i>daimyōs</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> his consolidation of power began what was known as the <a href="/wiki/Azuchi%E2%80%93Momoyama_period" title="Azuchi–Momoyama period">Azuchi–Momoyama period</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Honn%C5%8D-ji_Incident" title="Honnō-ji Incident">the death of Nobunaga</a> in 1582, his successor <a href="/wiki/Toyotomi_Hideyoshi" title="Toyotomi Hideyoshi">Toyotomi Hideyoshi</a> unified the nation in the early 1590s and launched <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasions_of_Korea_(1592%E2%80%9398)" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese invasions of Korea (1592–98)">two unsuccessful invasions of Korea in 1592 and 1597</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-courtiers_30-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courtiers-30">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_Ieyasu" title="Tokugawa Ieyasu">Tokugawa Ieyasu</a> served as <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Five_Elders" title="Council of Five Elders">regent</a> for Hideyoshi's son <a href="/wiki/Toyotomi_Hideyori" title="Toyotomi Hideyori">Toyotomi Hideyori</a> and used his position to gain political and military support.<sup id="cite_ref-Turnbull2011_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turnbull2011-41">[40]</a></sup> When open war broke out, Ieyasu defeated rival clans in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sekigahara" title="Battle of Sekigahara">Battle of Sekigahara</a> in 1600. He was appointed <i>shōgun</i> by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Go-Y%C5%8Dzei" title="Emperor Go-Yōzei">Emperor Go-Yōzei</a> in 1603 and established the <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a> at <a href="/wiki/Edo" title="Edo">Edo</a> (modern Tokyo).<sup id="cite_ref-closed_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-closed-42">[41]</a></sup> The shogunate enacted measures including <i><a href="/wiki/Buke_shohatto" title="Buke shohatto">buke shohatto</a></i>, as a code of conduct to control the autonomous <i>daimyōs</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> and in 1639 the isolationist <i><a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">sakoku</a></i> ("closed country") policy that spanned the two and a half centuries of tenuous political unity known as the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">Edo period</a> (1603–1868).<sup id="cite_ref-closed_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-closed-42">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Modern Japan's economic growth began in this period, resulting in <a href="/wiki/Kaid%C5%8D" title="Kaidō">roads</a> and water transportation routes, as well as financial instruments such as <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures contracts</a>, banking and insurance of the <a href="/wiki/Osaka_rice_brokers" class="mw-redirect" title="Osaka rice brokers">Osaka rice brokers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> The study of Western sciences (<i><a href="/wiki/Rangaku" title="Rangaku">rangaku</a></i>) continued through contact with the Dutch enclave in <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-closed_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-closed-42">[41]</a></sup> The Edo period gave rise to <i><a href="/wiki/Kokugaku" title="Kokugaku">kokugaku</a></i> ("national studies"), the study of Japan by the Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Meiji_tenno1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Meiji_tenno1.jpg/170px-Meiji_tenno1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Meiji_tenno1.jpg/255px-Meiji_tenno1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Meiji_tenno1.jpg/340px-Meiji_tenno1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="879" data-file-height="1203"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Meiji_tenno1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Emperor_Meiji" title="Emperor Meiji">Emperor Meiji</a> (<span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span lang="ja" title="Japanese-language text">明治天皇</span></span>, <i>Meiji-tennō</i>; 1852–1912)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1854, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_C._Perry" title="Matthew C. Perry">Commodore Matthew Perry</a> and the "<a href="/wiki/Black_Ships" title="Black Ships">Black Ships</a>" of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> forced the opening of Japan to the outside world with the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Kanagawa" title="Convention of Kanagawa">Convention of Kanagawa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-closed_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-closed-42">[41]</a></sup> Subsequent similar treaties with other Western countries brought economic and political crises.<sup id="cite_ref-closed_42-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-closed-42">[41]</a></sup> The resignation of the <i>shōgun</i> led to the <a href="/wiki/Boshin_War" title="Boshin War">Boshin War</a> and the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_the_han_system" title="Abolition of the han system">centralized state</a> nominally unified under the emperor (the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Restoration" title="Meiji Restoration">Meiji Restoration</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Adopting Western political, judicial, and military institutions, the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Japan" title="Cabinet of Japan">Cabinet</a> organized the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_(Japan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council (Japan)">Privy Council</a>, introduced the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Constitution" title="Meiji Constitution">Meiji Constitution</a>, and assembled the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">Imperial Diet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-modernnation_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modernnation-48">[47]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Meiji era">Meiji era</a> (1868–1912), the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> emerged as the most developed nation in Asia and as an industrialized world power that pursued military conflict to expand its sphere of influence.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> After victories in the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a> (1894–1895) and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> (1904–1905), Japan gained control of Taiwan, Korea and the southern half of <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-modernnation_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modernnation-48">[47]</a></sup> The Japanese population doubled from 35 million in 1873 to 70 million by 1935, with a significant shift to urbanization.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-excesses_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-54">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The early 20th century saw a period of <a href="/wiki/Taish%C5%8D_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Taishō period">Taishō democracy</a> (1912–1926) overshadowed by increasing <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">expansionism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_militarism" title="Japanese militarism">militarization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ramesh_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramesh-56">[55]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Japan_during_World_War_I" title="Japan during World War I">World War I</a> allowed Japan, which joined the side of the victorious <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>, to capture <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">German possessions</a> in the Pacific and in China.<sup id="cite_ref-ramesh_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramesh-56">[55]</a></sup> The 1920s saw a political shift towards <a href="/wiki/Statism_in_Sh%C5%8Dwa_Japan" title="Statism in Shōwa Japan">statism</a>, a period of lawlessness following the 1923 <a href="/wiki/Great_Tokyo_Earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Tokyo Earthquake">Great Tokyo Earthquake</a>, the passing of <a href="/wiki/Peace_Preservation_Law#Public_Security_Preservation_Law_of_1925" title="Peace Preservation Law">laws against political dissent</a>, and a series of <a href="/wiki/May_15_Incident" title="May 15 Incident">attempted coups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-excesses_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> This process accelerated during the 1930s, spawning a number of radical nationalist groups that shared a hostility to liberal democracy and a dedication to expansion in Asia. In 1931, Japan <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">invaded and occupied Manchuria</a>; following <a href="/wiki/Lytton_Report" title="Lytton Report">international condemnation of the occupation</a>, it resigned from the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> two years later.<sup id="cite_ref-Inc1945_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inc1945-59">[58]</a></sup> In 1936, Japan signed the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Comintern_Pact" title="Anti-Comintern Pact">Anti-Comintern Pact</a> with <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>; the 1940 <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a> made it one of the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-excesses_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-54">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Empire of Japan invaded other parts of China in 1937, precipitating the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (1937–1945).<sup id="cite_ref-Paine2012_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paine2012-60">[59]</a></sup> In 1940, the Empire <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_French_Indochina" title="Japanese invasion of French Indochina">invaded French Indochina</a>, after which the United States placed an oil embargo on Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-excesses_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> On December 7–8, 1941, Japanese forces carried out surprise <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attacks on Pearl Harbor</a>, as well as on <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> forces in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Malaya" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Malaya">Malaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Singapore_(1941)" title="Bombing of Singapore (1941)">Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hong_Kong" title="Battle of Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, among others, beginning <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">World War II in the Pacific</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> Throughout areas occupied by Japan during the war, numerous abuses were committed against local inhabitants, with many forced into <a href="/wiki/Comfort_women" title="Comfort women">sexual slavery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> victories during the next four years, which culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Soviet invasion of Manchuria">Soviet invasion of Manchuria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki</a> in 1945, Japan agreed to an <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">unconditional surrender</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> The war cost Japan <a href="/wiki/Japanese_colonial_empire" title="Japanese colonial empire">its colonies</a> and millions of lives.<sup id="cite_ref-excesses_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-54">[53]</a></sup> The Allies (led by the United States) repatriated millions of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_diaspora" title="Japanese diaspora">Japanese settlers</a> from their former colonies and military camps throughout Asia, largely eliminating the Japanese empire and its influence over the territories it conquered.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-phoenix_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-66">[65]</a></sup> The Allies convened the <a href="/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal_for_the_Far_East" title="International Military Tribunal for the Far East">International Military Tribunal for the Far East</a> to prosecute Japanese leaders for <a href="/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes" title="Japanese war crimes">war crimes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-phoenix_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-66">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1947, Japan adopted a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Japan" title="Constitution of Japan">constitution</a> emphasizing liberal democratic practices.<sup id="cite_ref-phoenix_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-66">[65]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan" title="Occupation of Japan">Allied occupation</a> ended with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco" title="Treaty of San Francisco">Treaty of San Francisco</a> in 1952,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> and Japan was granted membership in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-phoenix_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-66">[65]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Japanese_economic_miracle" title="Japanese economic miracle">period of record growth</a> propelled Japan to become the second-largest economy in the world;<sup id="cite_ref-phoenix_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-66">[65]</a></sup> this ended in the mid-1990s after the popping of an <a href="/wiki/Japanese_asset_price_bubble" title="Japanese asset price bubble">asset price bubble</a>, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Lost_Decade_(Japan)" title="Lost Decade (Japan)">"Lost Decade"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> On March 11, 2011, Japan suffered one of the <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">largest earthquakes in its recorded history</a>, triggering the <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes-tsunami_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-tsunami-69">[68]</a></sup> On May 1, 2019, after the historic <a href="/wiki/Abdication_of_Emperor_Akihito" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdication of Emperor Akihito">abdication of Emperor Akihito</a>, his son <a href="/wiki/Naruhito" title="Naruhito">Naruhito</a> became Emperor, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Reiwa" title="Reiwa">Reiwa</a> era.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Japan" title="Geography of Japan">Geography of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Japan" title="Geology of Japan">Geology of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg/170px-Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg/255px-Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg/340px-Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1638" data-file-height="2092"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">Japanese archipelago</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan comprises 6852 islands extending along the <a href="/wiki/Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific">Pacific</a> coast of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. It stretches over 3000&nbsp;km (1900&nbsp;mi) northeast–southwest from the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> to the <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-water_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-water-71">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> The county's five main islands, from north to south, are <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shikoku" title="Shikoku">Shikoku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Island" title="Okinawa Island">Okinawa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands" title="Ryukyu Islands">Ryukyu Islands</a>, which include Okinawa, are a chain to the south of Kyushu. The <a href="/wiki/Nanp%C5%8D_Islands" title="Nanpō Islands">Nanpō Islands</a> are south and east of the main islands of Japan. Together they are often known as the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">Japanese archipelago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan's territory is 377,975.24&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (145,937.06&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-area-2019_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-area-2019-3">[2]</a></sup> Japan has the sixth longest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_length_of_coastline" title="List of countries by length of coastline">coastline</a> in the world at 29,751&nbsp;km (18,486&nbsp;mi). Because of its far-flung outlying islands, Japan has the sixth largest <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone_of_Japan" title="Exclusive economic zone of Japan">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> in the world, covering 4,470,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,730,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-75">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of its mountainous terrain, approximately 67% of Japan's land is uninhabitable.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> The habitable zones, mainly in coastal areas, have extremely high population densities: Japan is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population density">most densely populated countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, approximately 0.5% of Japan's total area is <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">reclaimed land</a> (umetatechi).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan is substantially prone to earthquakes, <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> and volcanoes because of its location along the Pacific Ring of Fire.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> It has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_disaster_risk" title="List of countries by natural disaster risk">17th highest natural disaster risk</a> as measured in the 2016 World Risk Index.<sup id="cite_ref-wri_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wri-82">[81]</a></sup> Japan has 111 active volcanoes.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> Destructive earthquakes, often resulting in tsunami, occur several times each century;<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/1923_Great_Kant%C5%8D_earthquake" title="1923 Great Kantō earthquake">1923 Tokyo earthquake</a> killed over 140,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> More recent major quakes are the 1995 <a href="/wiki/Great_Hanshin_earthquake" title="Great Hanshin earthquake">Great Hanshin earthquake</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">2011 Tōhoku earthquake</a>, which triggered a large tsunami.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes-tsunami_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-tsunami-69">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Japan#Climate" title="Geography of Japan">Geography of Japan §&nbsp;Climate</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg/220px-Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg/330px-Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg/440px-Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5083" data-file-height="3389"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sakurajima_at_Sunset.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sakurajima" title="Sakurajima">Sakurajima</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate of Japan is predominantly temperate but varies greatly from north to south. The northernmost region, Hokkaido, has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> with long, cold winters and very warm to cool summers. <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is not heavy, but the islands usually develop deep snowbanks in the winter.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-86">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a> region on Honshu's west coast, northwest winter winds bring heavy snowfall during winter. In the summer, the region sometimes experiences extremely hot temperatures because of the <a href="/wiki/Foehn_wind" title="Foehn wind">foehn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Highland_(Japan)" title="Central Highland (Japan)">Central Highland</a> has a typical inland humid continental climate, with large temperature differences between summer and winter. The mountains of the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%ABgoku_region" title="Chūgoku region">Chūgoku</a> and Shikoku regions shelter the <a href="/wiki/Seto_Inland_Sea" title="Seto Inland Sea">Seto Inland Sea</a> from seasonal winds, bringing mild weather year-round.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-86">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Pacific coast features a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> climate that experiences milder winters with occasional snowfall and hot, humid summers because of the southeast seasonal wind. The Ryukyu and Nanpō Islands have a <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical climate</a>, with warm winters and hot summers. Precipitation is very heavy, especially during the rainy season.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-86">[85]</a></sup> The main <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_rainy_season" title="East Asian rainy season">rainy season</a> begins in early May in Okinawa, and the rain front gradually moves north. In late summer and early autumn, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">typhoons</a> often bring heavy rain.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> According to the Environment Ministry, heavy rainfall and increasing temperatures have caused problems in the agricultural industry and elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-climatechange_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climatechange-89">[88]</a></sup> The highest temperature ever measured in Japan, 41.1&nbsp;°C (106.0&nbsp;°F), was recorded on July 23, 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> and repeated on August 17, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Japan" title="Wildlife of Japan">Wildlife of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan has nine forest <a href="/wiki/Ecoregions_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecoregions in Japan">ecoregions</a> which reflect the climate and geography of the islands. They range from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">subtropical moist broadleaf forests</a> in the Ryūkyū and <a href="/wiki/Bonin_Islands" title="Bonin Islands">Bonin Islands</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests">temperate broadleaf and mixed forests</a> in the mild climate regions of the main islands, to <a href="/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest" title="Temperate coniferous forest">temperate coniferous forests</a> in the cold, winter portions of the northern islands.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Japan has over 90,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Japan" title="Wildlife of Japan">wildlife</a> as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup id="cite_ref-Sakurai2019_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sakurai2019-93">[92]</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bear</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_macaque" title="Japanese macaque">Japanese macaque</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_raccoon_dog" title="Japanese raccoon dog">Japanese raccoon dog</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Small_Japanese_field_mouse" title="Small Japanese field mouse">small Japanese field mouse</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_giant_salamander" title="Japanese giant salamander">Japanese giant salamander</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A large network of <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Japan" title="List of national parks of Japan">national parks</a> has been established to protect important areas of flora and fauna as well as 52 <a href="/wiki/Ramsar_sites_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramsar sites in Japan">Ramsar wetland sites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites in Japan">Four sites</a> have been inscribed on the UNESCO World Heritage List for their outstanding natural value.<sup id="cite_ref-unesco1_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco1-97">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Japan" title="Environmental issues in Japan">Environmental issues in Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Japan" title="Climate change in Japan">Climate change in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg/220px-Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg/330px-Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg/440px-Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="2133"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Autumn <a href="/wiki/Maple_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Maple tree">maple leaves</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Momiji" class="mw-redirect" title="Momiji">momiji</a></i>) at <a href="/wiki/Kong%C5%8Dbu-ji" title="Kongōbu-ji">Kongōbu-ji</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mount_K%C5%8Dya" title="Mount Kōya">Mount Kōya</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the period of rapid economic growth after World War II, environmental policies were downplayed by the government and industrial corporations; as a result, <a href="/wiki/Four_Big_Pollution_Diseases_of_Japan" title="Four Big Pollution Diseases of Japan">environmental pollution</a> was widespread in the 1950s and 1960s. Responding to rising concern, the government introduced environmental protection laws in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">oil crisis in 1973</a> also encouraged the efficient use of energy because of Japan's lack of natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, more than 22 coal-fired power plants are planned for construction in Japan, following the switching-off of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Japan" title="Nuclear power in Japan">Japan's nuclear fleet</a> after the 2011 Fukushima nuclear disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Japan ranks 20th in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a>, which measures a nation's commitment to environmental sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Japan is the world's fifth largest emitter of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-climatechange_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climatechange-89">[88]</a></sup> As the host and signatory of the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a>, Japan is under treaty obligation to reduce its carbon dioxide emissions and to take other steps to curb climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> In 2020 the government of Japan announced a target of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_neutrality" title="Carbon neutrality">carbon-neutrality</a> by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> Environmental issues include urban air pollution (<a href="/wiki/NOx" title="NOx">NOx</a>, suspended particulate matter, and toxics), <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">waste management</a>, water <a href="/wiki/Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication">eutrophication</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nature_conservation" title="Nature conservation">nature conservation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Japan" title="Climate change in Japan">climate change</a>, chemical management and international co-operation for conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Japan" title="Politics of Japan">Politics of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Japan" title="Government of Japan">Government of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> in which the power of the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">Emperor</a> is limited to a ceremonial role.<sup id="cite_ref-euparl_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-105">[104]</a></sup> Executive power is instead wielded by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Japan" title="Prime Minister of Japan">Prime Minister of Japan</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Japan" title="Cabinet of Japan">Cabinet</a>, whose sovereignty is vested in the Japanese people.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-106">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Naruhito" title="Naruhito">Naruhito</a> is the Emperor of Japan, having succeeded his father <a href="/wiki/Akihito" title="Akihito">Akihito</a> upon his accession to the <a href="/wiki/Chrysanthemum_Throne" title="Chrysanthemum Throne">Chrysanthemum Throne</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-euparl_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-105">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg/220px-Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg/330px-Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg/440px-Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2561" data-file-height="1726"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Diet_Building" title="National Diet Building">National Diet Building</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan's legislative organ is the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">National Diet</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-euparl_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-105">[104]</a></sup> It consists of a lower <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Japan)" title="House of Representatives (Japan)">House of Representatives</a> with 465 seats, elected by popular vote every four years or when dissolved, and an upper <a href="/wiki/House_of_Councillors_(Japan)" title="House of Councillors (Japan)">House of Councillors</a> with 245 seats, whose popularly-elected members serve six-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> There is <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> for adults over 18 years of age,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> with a <a href="/wiki/Secret_ballot" title="Secret ballot">secret ballot</a> for all elected offices.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-106">[105]</a></sup> The prime minister as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> has the power to appoint and dismiss <a href="/wiki/Ministers_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministers of State">Ministers of State</a>, and is <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Investiture" title="Imperial Investiture">appointed</a> by the emperor after being designated from among the members of the Diet.<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> Elected in the <a href="/wiki/2020_Liberal_Democratic_Party_(Japan)_leadership_election" title="2020 Liberal Democratic Party (Japan) leadership election">2020 Japanese prime minister election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yoshihide_Suga" title="Yoshihide Suga">Yoshihide Suga</a> is Japan's prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Historically influenced by <a href="/wiki/Chinese_law" title="Chinese law">Chinese law</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Japan" title="Law of Japan">Japanese legal system</a> developed independently during the Edo period through texts such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kujikata_Osadamegaki" title="Kujikata Osadamegaki">Kujikata Osadamegaki</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-dean_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dean-110">[109]</a></sup> Since the late 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Japan" title="Judicial system of Japan">judicial system</a> has been largely based on the <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> of Europe, notably Germany. In 1896, Japan established a <a href="/wiki/Civil_code" title="Civil code">civil code</a> based on the German <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCrgerliches_Gesetzbuch" title="Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch">Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch</a>, which remains in effect with post–World War II modifications.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Japan" title="Constitution of Japan">Constitution of Japan</a>, adopted in 1947, is the oldest unamended constitution in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-anomalous-constitution_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anomalous-constitution-112">[111]</a></sup> Statutory law originates in the legislature, and the constitution requires that the emperor promulgate legislation passed by the Diet without giving him the power to oppose legislation. The main body of Japanese statutory law is called the <a href="/wiki/Six_Codes" title="Six Codes">Six Codes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dean_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dean-110">[109]</a></sup> Japan's court system is divided into four basic tiers: the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Japan" title="Supreme Court of Japan">Supreme Court</a> and three levels of lower courts.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Japan" title="Administrative divisions of Japan">Administrative divisions of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">Prefectures of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan is divided into <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">47 prefectures</a>, each overseen by an elected <a href="/wiki/Governor_(Japan)" title="Governor (Japan)">governor</a> and legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-euparl_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-105">[104]</a></sup> In the following table, the prefectures are grouped by <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Japan" title="List of regions of Japan">region</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> </p>

          <hr> <p>15.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Niigata_Prefecture" title="Niigata Prefecture">Niigata</a><br> 16.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Toyama_Prefecture" title="Toyama Prefecture">Toyama</a><br> 17.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Ishikawa_Prefecture" title="Ishikawa Prefecture">Ishikawa</a><br> 18.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fukui_Prefecture" title="Fukui Prefecture">Fukui</a><br> 19.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Yamanashi_Prefecture" title="Yamanashi Prefecture">Yamanashi</a><br> 20.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Nagano_Prefecture" title="Nagano Prefecture">Nagano</a><br> 21.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Gifu_Prefecture" title="Gifu Prefecture">Gifu</a><br> 22.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Shizuoka_Prefecture" title="Shizuoka Prefecture">Shizuoka</a><br> 23.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Aichi_Prefecture" title="Aichi Prefecture">Aichi</a> </p> </td>

        <tr> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em; padding-left:2em; vertical-align:top;"> 
          <div class="center">
           <b>
            <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#9579EF; color:black;">&nbsp;</span> <a href="/wiki/Kansai" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansai">Kansai</a></b>
          </div> 
          <hr> <p>24.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Mie_Prefecture" title="Mie Prefecture">Mie</a><br> 25.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Shiga_Prefecture" title="Shiga Prefecture">Shiga</a><br> 26.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Prefecture" title="Kyoto Prefecture">Kyoto</a><br> 27.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Osaka_Prefecture" title="Osaka Prefecture">Osaka</a><br> 28.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Hy%C5%8Dgo_Prefecture" title="Hyōgo Prefecture">Hyōgo</a><br> 29.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Nara_Prefecture" title="Nara Prefecture">Nara</a><br> 30.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Wakayama_Prefecture" title="Wakayama Prefecture">Wakayama</a> </p> </td> 
         <td style="padding-right:1em; vertical-align:top;"> 
          <div class="center">
           <b>
            <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#EFB179; color:black;">&nbsp;</span> <a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%ABgoku_region" title="Chūgoku region">Chūgoku</a></b>
          </div>
