      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Japan" title="Foreign relations of Japan">Foreign relations of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/260px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/390px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/520px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3861" data-file-height="2574"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Japan is a member of both the <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a> and the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G20</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A member state of the United Nations since 1956, Japan is one of the <a href="/wiki/G4_nations" title="G4 nations">G4 nations</a> seeking reform of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Japan is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">G7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">APEC</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Free_Trade_Area#ASEAN_Plus_Three" title="ASEAN Free Trade Area">ASEAN Plus Three</a>", and is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-terada_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terada-116">[115]</a></sup> It is the world's fifth largest donor of <a href="/wiki/Official_development_assistance" title="Official development assistance">official development assistance</a>, donating US$9.2 billion in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> In 2017, Japan had the fifth largest diplomatic network in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-global-diplomacy-index_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global-diplomacy-index-118">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan has close economic and military relations with the United States, with which it maintains a <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Mutual_Cooperation_and_Security_between_the_United_States_and_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Mutual Cooperation and Security between the United States and Japan">security alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-us-relations_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us-relations-119">[118]</a></sup> The United States is a major market for Japanese exports and a major source of Japanese imports, and is committed to defending the country, with military bases in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-us-relations_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us-relations-119">[118]</a></sup> Japan signed a security pact with Australia in March 2007<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> and with India in October 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan's relationship with South Korea had historically been strained because of Japan's treatment of Koreans during <a href="/wiki/Korea_under_Japanese_rule" title="Korea under Japanese rule">Japanese colonial rule</a>, particularly over the issue of comfort women. In 2015, Japan agreed to settle the comfort women dispute with South Korea by issuing a formal apology and paying money to the surviving comfort women.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Japan is a major importer of Korean music (<a href="/wiki/K-pop" title="K-pop">K-pop</a>), television (<a href="/wiki/Korean_drama" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean drama">K-dramas</a>), and other cultural products.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan is engaged in several territorial disputes with its neighbors. Japan contests Russia's control of the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands_dispute" title="Kuril Islands dispute">Southern Kuril Islands</a>, which were occupied by the Soviet Union in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> South Korea's control of the <a href="/wiki/Liancourt_Rocks" title="Liancourt Rocks">Liancourt Rocks</a> is acknowledged but not accepted as they are claimed by Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-takeshima_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-takeshima-126">[125]</a></sup> Japan has strained relations with China and Taiwan over the <a href="/wiki/Senkaku_Islands" title="Senkaku Islands">Senkaku Islands</a> and the status of <a href="/wiki/Okinotorishima" title="Okinotorishima">Okinotorishima</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Forces" title="Japan Self-Defense Forces">Japan Self-Defense Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_(JMSDF)_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_(DDG_173)_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_(JMSDF)_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_(DDG_173)_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force">JMSDF</a> <a href="/wiki/Kong%C5%8D_class_destroyer" class="mw-redirect" title="Kongō class destroyer"><i>Kongō</i> class destroyer</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan is the second-highest-ranked Asian country in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a> 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> Japan maintains one of the largest military budgets of any country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> The country's military (the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Forces" title="Japan Self-Defense Forces">Japan Self-Defense Forces</a>) is restricted by <a href="/wiki/Article_9_of_the_Japanese_Constitution" title="Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution">Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution</a>, which renounces Japan's right to declare war or use military force in international disputes.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> The military is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Defense (Japan)">Ministry of Defense</a>, and primarily consists of the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Ground_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Ground Self-Defense Force">Japan Ground Self-Defense Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force">Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Air_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Air Self-Defense Force">Japan Air Self-Defense Force</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Iraq_Reconstruction_and_Support_Group" title="Japanese Iraq Reconstruction and Support Group">deployment of troops to Iraq</a> and Afghanistan marked the first overseas use of Japan's military since World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Japan" title="Government of Japan">Government of Japan</a> has been making changes to its security policy which include the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Council_(Japan)" title="National Security Council (Japan)">National Security Council</a>, the adoption of the National Security Strategy, and the development of the National Defense Program Guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan's_Security_Policy_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan's_Security_Policy-132">[131]</a></sup> In May 2014, Prime Minister Shinzō Abe said Japan wanted to shed the passiveness it has maintained since the end of World War II and take more responsibility for regional security.<sup id="cite_ref-JapanAsia_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JapanAsia-133">[132]</a></sup> Recent tensions, particularly with North Korea and China, have reignited the debate over the status of the JSDF and its relation to Japanese society.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_law_enforcement">Domestic law enforcement</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Japan" title="Law enforcement in Japan">Law enforcement in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Domestic security in Japan is provided mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Prefectural_police_department" title="Prefectural police department">prefectural police departments</a>, under the oversight of the <a href="/wiki/National_Police_Agency_(Japan)" title="National Police Agency (Japan)">National Police Agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> As the central coordinating body for the Prefectural Police Departments, the National Police Agency is administered by the <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Safety_Commission_(Japan)" title="National Public Safety Commission (Japan)">National Public Safety Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NPA1977-2_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPA1977-2-138">[137]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Special_Assault_Team" title="Special Assault Team">Special Assault Team</a> comprises national-level <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a> tactical units that cooperate with territorial-level <a href="/wiki/Riot_Police_Unit#Specialist_squads" title="Riot Police Unit">Anti-Firearms Squads and Counter-NBC Terrorism Squads</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WP_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-139">[138]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Coast_Guard" title="Japan Coast Guard">Japan Coast Guard</a> guards territorial waters surrounding Japan and uses surveillance and control countermeasures against smuggling, marine environmental crime, poaching, piracy, spy ships, unauthorized foreign fishing vessels, and illegal immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Firearm_and_Sword_Possession_Control_Law" title="Firearm and Sword Possession Control Law">Firearm and Sword Possession Control Law</a> strictly regulates the civilian ownership of guns, swords and other weaponry.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a>, among the member states of the UN that report statistics as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the incidence rates of violent crimes such as murder, abduction, sexual violence and robbery are very low in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Japan" title="Economy of Japan">Economy of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg/170px-The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg/255px-The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg/340px-The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1388" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Tokyo_Stock_Exchange_-_main_room_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Stock_Exchange" title="Tokyo Stock Exchange">Tokyo Stock Exchange</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan is the third largest national economy in the world, after the United States and China, in terms of <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> and the fourth largest national economy in the world, after the United States, China and India, in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan's <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">public debt</a> was estimated at around 230 percent of its annual gross domestic product, the largest of any rated nation,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> and Japan's labor force consisted of 67 million workers.<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> Japan has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_unemployment_rate" title="List of countries by unemployment rate">low unemployment rate</a> of around 2.4 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> Around 16 percent of the population were below the poverty line in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan's exports amounted to 18.5% of GDP in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan's main export markets were the United States (19.8 percent) and China (19.1 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> Its main exports are motor vehicles, iron and steel products, semiconductors and auto parts.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-75">[74]</a></sup> Japan's main import markets as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> were China (23.5 percent), the United States (11 percent), and Australia (6.3 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> Japan's main imports are machinery and equipment, fossil fuels, foodstuffs, chemicals, and raw materials for its industries.<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan ranks 29th of 190 countries in the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">ease of doing business index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> The Japanese variant of capitalism has many distinct features: <a href="/wiki/Keiretsu" title="Keiretsu">keiretsu</a> enterprises are influential, and <a href="/wiki/Permanent_employment" title="Permanent employment">lifetime employment</a> and seniority-based career advancement are common in the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_work_environment" title="Japanese work environment">Japanese work environment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd2008_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd2008-153">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> Japan has a large <a href="/wiki/Cooperative" title="Cooperative">cooperative</a> sector, with three of the ten largest cooperatives in the world, including the largest <a href="/wiki/Consumer_cooperative" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer cooperative">consumer cooperative</a> and the largest <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_cooperative" title="Agricultural cooperative">agricultural cooperative</a> in the world as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan ranks highly for <a href="/wiki/Competition_(companies)" class="mw-redirect" title="Competition (companies)">competitiveness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a>. It is ranked sixth in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a> for 2015–2016.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_fishery">Agriculture and fishery</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture,_forestry,_and_fishing_in_Japan" title="Agriculture, forestry, and fishing in Japan">Agriculture, forestry, and fishing in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu,_Japan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/220px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/330px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/440px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu,_Japan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Rice_paddy" class="mw-redirect" title="Rice paddy">rice paddy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aizu" title="Aizu">Aizu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Prefecture" title="Fukushima Prefecture">Fukushima Prefecture</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Japanese agricultural sector accounts for about 1.2% of the total country's GDP as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-sec_107-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-107">[106]</a></sup> Only 11.5% of Japan's land is suitable for cultivation.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Because of this lack of arable land, a system of <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(earthworks)" title="Terrace (earthworks)">terraces</a> is used to farm in small areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Urbanites_Help_Sustain_Japan's_Historic_Rice_Paddy_Terraces_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Urbanites_Help_Sustain_Japan's_Historic_Rice_Paddy_Terraces-159">[158]</a></sup> This results in one of the world's highest levels of crop yields per unit area, with an agricultural self-sufficiency rate of about 50% as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> Japan's small agricultural sector is highly subsidized and <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_Protectionism_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Agricultural Protectionism in Japan">protected</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> There has been a growing concern about farming as farmers are aging with a difficult time finding successors.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan ranked seventh in the world in <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_by_country" title="Fishing industry by country">tonnage of fish caught</a> and captured 3,167,610 metric tons of fish in 2016, down from an annual average of 4,000,000 tons over the previous decade.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> Japan maintains one of the world's largest fishing fleets and accounts for nearly 15% of the global catch,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-75">[74]</a></sup> prompting critiques that Japan's fishing is leading to depletion in fish stocks such as <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> Japan has sparked controversy by supporting commercial <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Japan" title="Whaling in Japan">whaling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_in_Japan" title="Manufacturing in Japan">Manufacturing in Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry_in_Japan" title="Electronics industry in Japan">Electronics industry in Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Japan" title="Automotive industry in Japan">Automotive industry in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/220px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/330px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/440px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5019" data-file-height="2492"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A plug-in <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid car</a> manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>. Japan is the third-largest maker of automobiles in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-166">[165]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan has a large industrial capacity and is home to some of the "largest and most technologically advanced producers of motor vehicles, <a href="/wiki/Machine_tool" title="Machine tool">machine tools</a>, steel and nonferrous metals, ships, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">chemical substances</a>, textiles, and <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processed foods</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-cia_75-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-75">[74]</a></sup> Japan's industrial sector makes up approximately 27.5% of its GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_75-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-75">[74]</a></sup> The country's manufacturing output is the third highest in the world as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan is the third largest automobile producer in the world as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> and is home to <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, the world's largest automobile company.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-166">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> The Japanese shipbuilding industry faces competition from South Korea and China; a 2020 government initiative identified this sector as a target for increasing exports.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_and_tourism">Services and tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Trade_and_services_in_Japan" title="Trade and services in Japan">Trade and services in Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Japan" title="Tourism in Japan">Tourism in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan's service sector accounts for about 70% of its total economic output as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> Banking, retail, <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in Japan">transportation</a>, and telecommunications are all major industries, with companies such as Toyota, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_UFJ_Financial_Group" title="Mitsubishi UFJ Financial Group">Mitsubishi UFJ</a>, -<a href="/wiki/Nippon_Telegraph_and_Telephone" title="Nippon Telegraph and Telephone">NTT</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%86ON_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="ÆON (company)">ÆON</a>, <a href="/wiki/Softbank" class="mw-redirect" title="Softbank">Softbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hitachi" title="Hitachi">Hitachi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Itochu" title="Itochu">Itochu</a> listed as among the largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_Global_500_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_Global_500-171">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan attracted 31.9&nbsp;million international tourists in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> For inbound tourism, Japan was <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">ranked</a> 11th in the world in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> The 2017 <i><a href="/wiki/Travel_and_Tourism_Competitiveness_Report" title="Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report">Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report</a></i> ranked Japan 4th out of 141 countries, which was the highest in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Japan" title="Science and technology in Japan">Science and technology in Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Video gaming in Japan">Video gaming in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/220px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/330px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/440px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2039"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Experiment Module">Japanese Experiment Module</a> (Kibō) at the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan is a leading nation in <a href="/wiki/Scientific_research" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific research">scientific research</a>, particularly in the natural sciences and engineering. The country ranks twelfth among the most innovative countries in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Innovation_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloomberg Innovation Index">Bloomberg Innovation Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> Relative to gross domestic product, Japan's <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> budget is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_research_and_development_spending" title="List of countries by research and development spending">second highest in the world</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> with 867,000 researchers sharing a 19-trillion-yen research and development budget as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> The country has produced twenty-two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureates</a> in either physics, chemistry or medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> and three <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields medalists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan leads the world in <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a> production and use, supplying 55% of the world's 2017 total.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> Japan has the second highest number of researchers in science and technology per capita in the world with 14 per 1000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Japanese consumer electronics industry, once considered the strongest in the world, is in a state of decline as competition arises in countries like South Korea and China.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Video gaming in Japan">video gaming in Japan</a> remains a major industry. In 2014, Japan's consumer video game market grossed $9.6 billion, with $5.8 billion coming from mobile gaming.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Aerospace_Exploration_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency">Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency</a> is Japan's national <a href="/wiki/Space_agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Space agency">space agency</a>; it conducts space, planetary, and aviation research, and leads development of rockets and satellites.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> It is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Experiment Module">Japanese Experiment Module</a> (Kibō) was added to the station during <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> assembly flights in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">space probe</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Akatsuki_(spacecraft)" title="Akatsuki (spacecraft)">Akatsuki</a></i> was launched in 2010 and achieved orbit around Venus in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup> Japan's plans in <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> include building a <a href="/wiki/Colonization_of_the_Moon" title="Colonization of the Moon">moon base</a> and landing astronauts by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> In 2007, it launched lunar explorer <a href="/wiki/SELENE" title="SELENE">SELENE</a> (Selenological and Engineering Explorer) from <a href="/wiki/Tanegashima_Space_Center" title="Tanegashima Space Center">Tanegashima Space Center</a>. The largest lunar mission since the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a>, its purpose was to gather data on the <a href="/wiki/Moon#Formation" title="Moon">moon's origin and evolution</a>. The explorer entered a lunar orbit on October 4, 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> and was deliberately crashed into the Moon on June 11, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Japan" title="Transport in Japan">Transport in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Japan_Airlines,_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_(19455285040).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/220px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/330px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/440px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4678" data-file-height="3120"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Japan_Airlines,_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_(19455285040).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> of Japan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan has invested heavily in transportation infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> The country has approximately 1,200,000 kilometers (750,000 miles) of roads made up of 1,000,000 kilometers (620,000 miles) of city, town and village roads, 130,000 kilometers (81,000 miles) of prefectural roads, 54,736 kilometers (34,011 miles) of general national highways and 7641 kilometers (4748 miles) of national <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Japan" title="Expressways of Japan">expressways</a> as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since privatization in 1987,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_railway_companies_in_Japan" title="List of railway companies in Japan">dozens of Japanese railway companies</a> compete in regional and local passenger transportation markets; major companies include seven <a href="/wiki/Japan_Railways_Group" title="Japan Railways Group">JR</a> enterprises, <a href="/wiki/Kintetsu_Railway" title="Kintetsu Railway">Kintetsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seibu_Railway" title="Seibu Railway">Seibu Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keio_Corporation" title="Keio Corporation">Keio Corporation</a>. The high-speed <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">Shinkansen</a> (bullet trains) that connect major cities are known for their safety and punctuality.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are 175 airports in Japan as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_75-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-75">[74]</a></sup> The largest domestic airport, <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">Haneda Airport</a> in Tokyo, was <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">Asia's second-busiest airport</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> The Keihin and Hanshin superport hubs are among the largest in the world, at 7.98 and 5.22 million <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">TEU</a> respectively as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Japan" title="Energy in Japan">Energy in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_(8388173865).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/220px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/330px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/440px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2808" data-file-height="2132"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_(8388173865).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Kashiwazaki-Kariwa Nuclear Power Plant">Kashiwazaki-Kariwa Nuclear Power Plant</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 39% of energy in Japan was produced from petroleum, 25% from coal, 23% from natural gas, 3.5% from <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> and 1.5% from <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Japan" title="Nuclear power in Japan">nuclear power</a>. Nuclear power was down from 11.2 percent in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> By May 2012 all of the country's nuclear power plants had been taken offline because of ongoing public opposition following the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster in March 2011, though government officials continued to try to sway public opinion in favor of returning at least some to service.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sendai_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Sendai Nuclear Power Plant">Sendai Nuclear Power Plant</a> restarted in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> and since then several other nuclear power plants have been restarted.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> Japan lacks significant domestic reserves and has a heavy dependence on <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_imports" title="List of countries by oil imports">imported energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> The country has therefore aimed to diversify its sources and maintain high levels of energy efficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Japan" title="Water supply and sanitation in Japan">Water supply and sanitation in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Responsibility for the water and sanitation sector is shared between the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health,_Labour_and_Welfare_(Japan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Health, Labour and Welfare (Japan)">Ministry of Health, Labour and Welfare</a>, in charge of water supply for domestic use; the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Land,_Infrastructure,_Transport_and_Tourism_(Japan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism (Japan)">Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism</a>, in charge of water resources development as well as sanitation; the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Environment_(Japan)" title="Ministry of the Environment (Japan)">Ministry of the Environment</a>, in charge of ambient water quality and environmental preservation; and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs_and_Communications" title="Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications">Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications</a>, in charge of performance benchmarking of utilities.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> Access to an <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water source</a> is universal in Japan. About 98% of the population receives piped water supply from public utilities.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Japan" title="Demographics of Japan">Demographics of Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Japan" title="Ethnic groups of Japan">Ethnic groups of Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Japan" title="List of metropolitan areas in Japan">List of metropolitan areas in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG/220px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG/330px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG/440px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5999" data-file-height="3598"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a> is ranked as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">most populous metropolitan area</a> in the world.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan has a <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Demography of Japan">population</a> of 126.3 million,<sup id="cite_ref-SBJ-Population-June-2019_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBJ-Population-June-2019-206">[205]</a></sup> of which 124.8 million are Japanese nationals (2019).<sup id="cite_ref-Population-2019-124-mil_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-2019-124-mil-207">[206]</a></sup> In 2019, 92% of the total Japanese population lived in cities.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> The capital city Tokyo has a population of 13.8 million (2018).<sup id="cite_ref-toukei-metro_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toukei-metro-209">[208]</a></sup> It is part of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a>, the biggest <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">metropolitan area</a> in the world with 38,140,000 people (2016).<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-210">[209]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan's population is 98.1% ethnic Japanese as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_75-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-75">[74]</a></sup> with small populations of foreign workers.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> Primary minority groups include the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ainu_people" title="Ainu people">Ainu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryukyuan_people" title="Ryukyuan people">Ryukyuan people</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> as well as social minority groups like the <i><a href="/wiki/Burakumin" title="Burakumin">burakumin</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_Japan" title="Koreans in Japan">Zainichi Koreans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Japan" title="Chinese people in Japan">Chinese</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Japan" title="Filipinos in Japan">Filipinos</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup> Brazilians mostly <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Brazilian">of Japanese descent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup> and Peruvians mostly <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Peruvian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Peruvian">of Japanese descent</a> are among the small minority groups in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan has the second longest overall <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> at birth of any country in the world, at 84 years as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Aging_of_Japan" title="Aging of Japan">Japanese population is rapidly aging</a> as a result of a <a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_baby_boom" class="mw-redirect" title="Post–World War II baby boom">post–World War II baby boom</a> followed by a decrease in birth rates.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> over 20 percent of the population is over 65, and this is projected to rise to one in three by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-walia_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walia-221">[220]</a></sup> The changes in demographic structure have created a number of social issues, particularly a decline in workforce population and increase in the cost of social security benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-walia_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walia-221">[220]</a></sup> A growing number of younger Japanese are not marrying or remain childless.<sup id="cite_ref-walia_221-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walia-221">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> Japan's population is expected to drop to around 100 million by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Japan" title="Immigration to Japan">Immigration</a> and birth incentives are sometimes suggested as a solution to provide younger workers to support the nation's aging population.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> On April 1, 2019, Japan's revised immigration law was enacted, protecting the rights of foreign workers to help reduce labor shortages in certain sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup> </p>

         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Saitama_(city)" title="Saitama (city)">Saitama</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Saitama_Prefecture" title="Saitama Prefecture">Saitama</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">1,263,979</td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">20</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Okayama" title="Okayama">Okayama</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Okayama_Prefecture" title="Okayama Prefecture">Okayama</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">719,474 </td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Japan" title="Religion in Japan">Religion in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Itsukushima_Gate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Itsukushima_Gate.jpg/220px-Itsukushima_Gate.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Itsukushima_Gate.jpg/330px-Itsukushima_Gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Itsukushima_Gate.jpg/440px-Itsukushima_Gate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4200" data-file-height="2803"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Itsukushima_Gate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Torii" title="Torii">torii</a> of <a href="/wiki/Itsukushima_Shrine" title="Itsukushima Shrine">Itsukushima Shinto Shrine</a> near <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">Hiroshima</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Japan's constitution guarantees full religious freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-Inoue2007_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inoue2007-227">[226]</a></sup> Upper estimates suggest that 84–96 percent of the Japanese population subscribe to <a href="/wiki/Shinto" title="Shinto">Shinto</a> as its indigenous religion.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> However, these estimates are based on people <a href="/wiki/Danka_system" title="Danka system">affiliated</a> with a temple, rather than the number of true believers. Many Japanese people practice both Shinto and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>; they can either identify with both religions or describe themselves as non-religious or spiritual.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup> The level of participation in religious ceremonies as a cultural tradition remains high, especially during <a href="/wiki/Japanese_festivals" title="Japanese festivals">festivals</a> and occasions such as the <a href="/wiki/Hatsum%C5%8Dde" title="Hatsumōde">first shrine visit</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_New_Year" title="Japanese New Year">New Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> from China have also influenced Japanese beliefs and customs.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> was first introduced into Japan by Jesuit missions starting in 1549. Today, 1%<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[231]</a></sup> to 1.5% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Japan" title="Christianity in Japan">Christians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> Throughout the latest century, Western customs originally related to Christianity (including <a href="/wiki/Marriage_in_Japan" title="Marriage in Japan">Western style weddings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine's Day">Valentine's Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>) have become popular as secular customs among many Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 90% of those practicing <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Japan" title="Islam in Japan">Islam in Japan</a> are foreign-born migrants as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there were an estimated 105 <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> and 200,000 Muslims in Japan, 43,000 of which were ethnically Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup> Other minority religions include <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Japan" title="Hinduism in Japan">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith_in_Japan" title="Baháʼí Faith in Japan">Baháʼí Faith</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Animist" class="mw-redirect" title="Animist">animist</a> beliefs of the Ainu.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Japan" title="Languages of Japan">Languages of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese language</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_(5023366778).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_%285023366778%29.jpg/220px-%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_%285023366778%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_%285023366778%29.jpg/330px-%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_%285023366778%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_%285023366778%29.jpg/440px-%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_%285023366778%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%E8%B1%9A%E9%AA%A8%E3%82%89%E3%83%BC%E3%82%81%E3%82%93_%E5%8D%9A%E5%A4%9A%E5%A4%A9%E7%A5%9E_%E3%81%84%E3%82%89%E3%81%A3%E3%81%97%E3%82%83%E3%81%84_2010_(5023366778).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">Kanji</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hiragana" title="Hiragana">hiragana</a></i> signs
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Japanese_writing_system" title="Japanese writing system">Japanese writing</a> uses <a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">kanji</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_character" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese character">Chinese characters</a>) and two sets of <a href="/wiki/Kana" title="Kana">kana</a> (<a href="/wiki/Syllabary" title="Syllabary">syllabaries</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Cursive_script_(East_Asia)" title="Cursive script (East Asia)">cursive script</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radical_(Chinese_characters)" title="Radical (Chinese characters)">radical</a> of kanji), as well as the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_numerals" title="Arabic numerals">Arabic numerals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup> English instruction was made mandatory in Japanese elementary schools in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Besides Japanese, the <a href="/wiki/Ryukyuan_languages" title="Ryukyuan languages">Ryukyuan languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amami_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Amami language">Amami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kunigami_language" title="Kunigami language">Kunigami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Okinawan_language" title="Okinawan language">Okinawan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miyakoan_language" title="Miyakoan language">Miyako</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yaeyama_language" title="Yaeyama language">Yaeyama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yonaguni_language" title="Yonaguni language">Yonaguni</a>), part of the <a href="/wiki/Japonic_languages" title="Japonic languages">Japonic language family</a>, are spoken in the Ryukyu Islands chain.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> Few children learn these languages,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup> but local governments have sought to increase awareness of the traditional languages.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ainu_language" title="Ainu language">Ainu language</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolate</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Moribund_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Moribund language">moribund</a>, with only a few native speakers remaining as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[242]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Japan" title="Education in Japan">Education in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG/220px-Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG/330px-Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG/440px-Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_University_Entrance_Exam_Results_6.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Students celebrating after the announcement of the results of the <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_Japan#University_entrance" title="Higher education in Japan">entrance examinations</a> to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">University of Tokyo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Primary schools, secondary schools and universities were <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Empire_of_Japan" title="Education in the Empire of Japan">introduced</a> in 1872 as a result of the Meiji Restoration.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[243]</a></sup> Since the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_Law_of_Education" title="Fundamental Law of Education">Fundamental Law of Education</a>, compulsory education in Japan comprises <a href="/wiki/Elementary_schools_in_Japan" title="Elementary schools in Japan">elementary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_Japan#Junior_high_school" title="Secondary education in Japan">junior high school</a>, which together last for nine years.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[244]</a></sup> Almost all children continue their education at a three-year <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_Japan" title="Secondary education in Japan">senior high school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[245]</a></sup> The two top-ranking universities in Japan are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">University of Tokyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_University" title="Kyoto University">Kyoto University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[246]</a></sup> Starting in April 2016, various schools began the academic year with elementary school and junior high school integrated into one nine-year compulsory schooling program; <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Culture,_Sports,_Science_and_Technology" title="Ministry of Education, Culture, Sports, Science and Technology">MEXT</a> plans for this approach to be adopted nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a> coordinated by the OECD ranks the knowledge and skills of Japanese 15-year-olds as the third best in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-249">[248]</a></sup> Japan is one of the top-performing <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> countries in reading literacy, math and sciences with the average student scoring 529 and has one of the world's highest-educated labor forces among OECD countries.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto4_249-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-249">[248]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[250]</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan's public spending on education amounted to just 3.3 percent of its GDP, below the OECD average of 4.9 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup> In 2017, the country ranked third for the percentage of 25- to 64-year-olds that have attained tertiary education with 51 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-253">[252]</a></sup> Approximately 60 percent of Japanese aged 25 to 34 have some form of tertiary education qualification, and bachelor's degrees are held by 30.4 percent of Japanese aged 25 to 64, the second most in the OECD after South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-253">[252]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Japan" title="Health in Japan">Health in Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_care_system_in_Japan" title="Health care system in Japan">Health care system in Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Health care is provided by national and local governments. Payment for personal medical services is offered through a universal health insurance system that provides relative equality of access, with fees set by a government committee. People without insurance through employers can participate in a national health insurance program administered by local governments.<sup id="cite_ref-Ikegami2014_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ikegami2014-254">[253]</a></sup> Since 1973, all elderly persons have been covered by government-sponsored insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[254]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Japan <a href="/wiki/Suicide_in_Japan" title="Suicide in Japan">has one of the world's highest suicide rates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[255]</a></sup> Another significant public health issue is <a href="/wiki/Smoking_in_Japan" title="Smoking in Japan">smoking among Japanese men</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[256]</a></sup> Japan has the lowest rate of heart disease in the OECD, and the lowest level of dementia in the developed world.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[257]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Japan" title="Culture of Japan">Culture of Japan</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Japanese_popular_culture" title="Japanese popular culture">Japanese popular culture</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Contemporary Japanese culture combines influences from Asia, Europe and North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Haffner_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haffner-259">[258]</a></sup> Traditional Japanese arts include <a href="/wiki/Japanese_handicrafts" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese handicrafts">crafts</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Japanese_pottery_and_porcelain" title="Japanese pottery and porcelain">ceramics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimono" title="Kimono">textiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_lacquerware" title="Japanese lacquerware">lacquerware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_sword" title="Japanese sword">swords</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_traditional_dolls" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese traditional dolls">dolls</a>; performances of <a href="/wiki/Bunraku" title="Bunraku">bunraku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kabuki" title="Kabuki">kabuki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noh" title="Noh">noh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_traditional_dance" title="Japanese traditional dance">dance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rakugo" title="Rakugo">rakugo</a>; and other practices, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_tea_ceremony" title="Japanese tea ceremony">tea ceremony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ikebana" title="Ikebana">ikebana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_martial_arts" title="Japanese martial arts">martial arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_calligraphy" title="Japanese calligraphy">calligraphy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Origami" title="Origami">origami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onsen" title="Onsen">onsen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geisha" title="Geisha">Geisha</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Japanese_games" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Japanese games">games</a>. Japan has a developed system for the protection and promotion of both tangible and intangible <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Properties_of_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural Properties of Japan">Cultural Properties</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Treasures_of_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="National Treasures of Japan">National Treasures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[259]</a></sup> Twenty-two sites have been inscribed on the UNESCO World Heritage List, eighteen of which are of cultural significance.<sup id="cite_ref-unesco1_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco1-97">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Japanese_art" title="Japanese art">Japanese art</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Japanese_garden" title="Japanese garden">Japanese garden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_esthetics" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese esthetics">Japanese esthetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">Manga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_sculpture" title="Japanese sculpture">Japanese sculpture</a>
      </div>
